Some Basic Lessons
Mesoe Foris Kohgnaetnigs

Basic Expressions: (Foris Swertishins)

Yes: Shem
No: Nwok or Noy
Please: Pleje or Platoe
Thank you: Darlettoe Ina
You’re Welcome: Inaroe Koolome Or Inar Koolome
Thank you very much: Darlettoe Ina Koomoe Kintoe
That’s all right/
Don’t mention it:  Thet’s elltaj/ Odent jabran tet

GREETINGS: WELKNIGS
Good morning.          Mees Magan.
Good afternoon.        Mees ahflum sennestoe.
Good evening.            Mees vyonnig.
Good night.                 Mees Chelloe.
Goodbye.                     Mees chon.
See you later.               Orit Ina Vlit.
This is Mr./Mrs.            Thes est Stravij/Vostravij
How do you do?           Trow ode Ina ode? 
How are you?                Trow moe Ina.
Very well, Thanks.        Koomoe meram, Darlettoes.
And you?                        Ont/und Ina? 
How’s life?                     Trow’s felli?
Fine.                                Meon.
I beg your pardon?       Fe gach Inar norjahd?
Excuse me.
(may I get past?)           Paryan mohn. Yame Fe gat stint?
Sorry!                              Sonarsh!

QUESTIONS:  BLYQUINNS
Where?                           Thilla?
How?                               Trow?
When?                             Whan? 
What?                              Dhut?
Why?                                Vry?
Who?                                Hom? 
Which?                             Tord?

Where is?...   Thilla est?....           Where are?...  Thilla moe?...
Where can/or/may I find?...        Thilla dom/yame Fe remm?...
Where can I get?...                        Thilla dom Fe gat?....
How far?...                                      Trow kran?...
How long?...                                   Trow skwit?...
How much?...                               Trow kintoe?...
How many?...                               Trow numsu?....
How much does this cost?         Trow kintoe odes thes proesk?
When does… open/close?         Whan odes…endeb/larf?
What do you call this in suqellish?   Dhut ote Ina holell thes nin Suquis?
What does that mean?                       Dhut odes thet groon?
What does this word mean?             Dhut odes thes kail groon? 
DO YOU SPEAK…?     Ode Ina hoik…?
Do you speak English?                        Ode Ina hoik Ganyon?
Is there anyone here that speaks English?   Est silla onyplur hech thet hoiks Ganyon? 
Do you speak Suquellish?                   Ode Ina hoik Suquis? 
I don’t speak Suquellish.                     Fe ode nelt hoik Suquis.
Can you repeat that?                           Dom Ina rojinn thet? 
Can you say it more slowly?               Dom Ina soy tet rone thitly?
Can you spell it?                                   Dom Ina Tuskrib tet?
Can you translate this for me/us?    Dom Ina nidzkail thes rofe mohn/Oos?
I understand.                                      Fe dopanskad.
I don’t understand.                            Fe odent dopenskad.
Do you understand?                          Ode Ina dopanskad?  



Can/May          Dom/Yame
Can I have…?                              Rom Fe vase…?
Can we have…?                          Rom Woy vase…?
Can you show…?                        Rom Ina orm…?
(Me…?)                                        (mohn…?)
I can’t.                                          Fe rom nelt.
Can you tell me…?                     Rom Ina holell mohn…?
Can you help me?                      Rom Ina broon mohn?
Can I help you?                          Rom Fe broon Ina?
Can you direct me to…?           Rom Ina jorvil mohn ote…?

What do you want?        (Dhut ode Ina vont?)
I’d like…                                        Fe’d kile…
We’d like…                                   Woy’d kile…
Give me…                                     Gipe mohn…
Give it to me.                               Gipe tet ote mohn.
Bring me…                                    Rim mohn…
Bring it to me.                              Rim tet ote mohn.
Show me…                                    Orm mohn…
Show it to me.                              Orm tet ote mohn.
I’m looking for…                           Fe’k oritnig rofe…
I’m hungry…                                  Fe’k reUngi…
I’m thirsty…                                 Fe’k japqahoy.
I’m tired…                                    Fe’k snooli.
I’m lost…                                      Fe’k flarst.
It’s important…                           Tet’s herrayik.
It’s Urgent…                                 Tet’s urtwen.
Hurry up…                                    Fleecho pun!

It is/there is       (Tet est/thilla est)
It is…                                    Tet est.
Is it?                                     Est tet?
It isn’t…                               Tet Est nelt.
Here it is.                             Hech tet est. 
Here they are.                    Hech thoy moe.
There is/are…                     Thilla est/moe
Is there/Are there…           Est thilla/ Moe thilla
There isn’t (any)…              Thilla est nelt opee.
There aren’t (any)…           Thilla moe nelt opee.

Adjectives:  
(Folskribshins):
Big/small                             Huge/posmall
Quick/slow                          speet/thit
Cheap/expensive                                 hort/yonponsif
Hot/cold                                                flam/chize
Full/empty                                            lum/dochi
Easy/difficult                                        yaysi/hardokun
Heavy/ light                                          wonry/yosh
Open/shut                                             endeb/larf
Right/wrong                                          leet or taj/bodu
Old/new                                                 krayd/wiss
Old/young                                              krayd/Sannewj
Next/last                                                 pext/grig
Beautiful/ugly                                        Brewwin/Posserj
Occupied/free/empty                          ditrahlayt/gallam/dochi
Good/bad                                               mees/roht
Friend/enemy                                        dinroo/merkefir
Better/worse                                          glappy/varsarse
Early/late                                                ornty/vlit
Near/far                                                  Quone/kran
Left/right                                                 loit/tahj

Quantities: (Numbrodys):
A little…                                             E possmall
A lot…                                                E gim
A few…                                            E mel
Much/many                                   Kintoe/numsu
More…                                            rone…
Less…                                              kass…
Enough/too much                        kashin/oot kintoe
Some/any                                      mesoe/onee

A few more useful words…                  E mel rone ursfill kails…
At…                                                 Et or Oht…
On…                                                Noy…
In…                                                  Nin…
To…                                                 Ote…
After…                                            Ahflum…
Before…                                         Borofe…
For…                                               Rofe
From…                                            Fram
Go…                                                Goy
With…                                             Seth
Without…                                       Sethtog
Through…                                       Thrope
Towards…                                       Twids
Until…                                              Ointeel
During…                                          Makquin 
Next to…                                         Pext ote
Behind…                                          Bozurk
Between…                                       Poemet or botwix
Since…                                              Kak
Above…                                            Skykah
Below…                                             Pahki
Over…                                                Jage
Under…                                              Pahkor
Inside…                                               Nindoy
Outside…                                            Togdoy
Up…                                                     Pun or Ip
Down…                                                Drob
Here…                                                  Hech
There…                                                 Sillah
And…                                                    Und or ont
Or…                                                       Oor
But…                                                      Pang
Not…                                                      Nelt
Never…                                                  Verrop
Nothing…                                               Noyoth
None…                                                    Noke
Very…                                                      Koomoe
Too…                                                        Oot
Yet…                                                         Yat
Soon…                                                      foon
Now…                                                       Kraym
Only…                                                       Anay
Then…                                                      Tharn
Perhaps…                                                 Yamips
Maybe…                                                   Yaemboe

Visitors: Plugasors: (Arrivals, Hiskoddells)
Do you have a passport?....................Ode Ina vase E stingort?
Here’s my passport…………………………..Hech est moy stingort.
I’ll be staying…………………………………….Fe’ll boe greernig….
　　　　A day………………………………………………..E estoe.
　　　　A week……………………………………………..E estoke.
　　　　A month……………………………………………E enstron.
　　　　A year……………………………………………….E Parrok.
　　　　I don’t know how long I’ll be visiting…Fe odent kognah trow skwit        Fe’ll boe plugasornig.

I’m here on business…………………………………Fe hech noy sanziben.
I’m just passing through.                              Fe’k roy stinnig thrope.
If things become difficult…   Aff drings boklum hardokun…
I’m sorry, I don’t understand……….Fe’k sonarsh, Fe ode nelt dopanskad.
Does anyone speak English?           Odes onyplur hoik Ganyon?
It’s for my personal use.                   Tet’s rofe moy pajoeni Urse.
Baggage:  (Gachog)
Porter! Please take this luggage.     Hoeleer! Pleje nach thes gachog.
That’s mine.                                         Thet’s moin.
That’s my suitcase.                             Thet’s moy lantsebrif.
There is one piece missing.               Thilla est plur silm mussnig.
Please take this to the bus/taxi       Pleje klake thes ote de tran/rixi
HOTEL: (STRAKENZIE)
Can you suggest a hotel?                  Rom Ina koggest E strakenzie?
My name is…                                       Moy meo est…
Do you have rooms open?                Ode Ina vase blores endeb?
I’d like a single/double room.           Fe’k kile E sawkat/tanbol blore.
I’d like a room.                                    Fe’k kile E blore.
It must be quiet.                                 Tet yad boe slunjit.
It must have a bath/shower.             Tet yad vase E kleant/drizzer
With twin beds…                                 Seth tangee kodjis…
With a balcony…                                  Seth E bo’ahkni…
Is there…                                                Est thilla…
Air conditioning?                                    Bruth steepolinnig? 
A radio/television?                                 E freqinnoe/kayleorich?
Laundry service?                                     Webenny tanrove?
Hot water?                                                Flam/Drot plaquar?
Running water?                                       Tratnig plaquar?
A private toilet?                                       E hepsig kolear?
Could you put an extra bed in the room?  
Rom Ina yun en inska kodj nin de blore?

How much?      Trow kintoe?
What’s the price?                                     Dhut’s de sum?
Per night?                                                  Han de chello?
Per week?                                                  Han de estoke?
For bed and breakfast?                           Rofe kodj ont magangarb? 
Without meals?                                        Sethtog garbs?
When is breakfast?                                  Whan est magangarb? 
Is there a discount for children?           Est silla E dossbram rofe bolissen?
Do you charge for the baby?                 Ode Ina jarg rofe de enfon?
That’s too expensive!                              Thet’s oot yonponsif!
Do you have anything cheaper?            Ode Ina vase onydring horter? 

Decision:  domashin

Basic General expressions in Commerce: 
Where…
Where is a good…                                         Thilla est E mees…
Where can I find…                                         Thilla rom Fe Remm…
Where’s the main shopping area?             Thilla’s De nain Troennig
                                                                          Haxeo?
Is it far from here?                                         Est tet kran frame hech?
How do I get there?                                       Trow ode Fe Gat silla?
Service:
Can you help me?                                    Rom Ina broon mohn?
I’m just looking.                                        Fe’k roy oritnig.
I want…                                                      Fe vont…
Can you show me…                                 Rom Ina orm mohn…
Do you sell…                                             Ode Ina svin…
Will you buy…                                          Dell Ina tarn…
I’d like to buy…                                        Fe’d kile ote tarn…
Do you have any…                                   Ode Ina vase ony…
Where’s the department?                     Thilla’s de tarpidant?
Where’s the elevator/escalator?          Thilla est de grut?
That one… Thet plur…  
That/Those…                                             Thet/Thuse…
The one in the window.                           De plur nin de Tamdow.
In the display case…                                 Nin de dosspojoe sebrif…

Expensive.                                                   Yonponsif.
Preferences:

                                                                       Rone?

Cheaper/better                                            Horter/Glappy
Larger/smaller                                              Jarker/Possmallor
HOW MUCH: (TROW KINTOE):
How much is this?                                       Trow kintoe est thes?
I don’t understand.                                      Fe ode nelt dopanskad.
Please write it down.                                   Pleje, skrib tet drob.
I don’t want to spend more than…            Fe odent vont ote poynd rone..
Pons.                                                               Thon…Pons.
Decision:
It’s not really what I want.                       Tet’s nelt molly dhut Fe vont.
No, I don’t like it.                                       Nwok. Fe odent kile tet.
I’ll take it!                                                    Fe’ll klake tet!
Ordering:
Can you order it for me?                           Rom Ina bakkan tet rofe mohn? 
How long will it take?                                 Trow skwit dell tet klake? 
Delivery:
I’ll take it with me.                                       Fe’ll klake tet seth mohn.
Deliver it to the…hotel.                              Nahkleet tet ote de…strakanzie.
Send it to this address.                               Trepp tet ote thes streplise.
Paying:
Where do I pay?                                           Thilla ode Fe lat?
How much is it?                                            Trow kintoe est tet?
Can I pay with debit card?                           Ode Ina lat seth debit parch?
Can I pay with credit card?                          Ode Ina lat seth jarg parch? 
Do you accept…                                              Ode Ina impraze…
Dollars?                                                            Dolliars?
Pounds?                                                            Plahjis?
Only Suquellish Pons?                                    Ony, Suquis Pons? 
Checks?                                                             Krafes?
Digital Dollars?                                                 Nerboed Dolliars?
I think you made a mistake on my bill.    Fe Kognah Ina mannuted 
                                                                       E musklake noy mohn invoy.
Anything else?
No, thanks. That’s all.                          Nwok, darlettoes. Thet’s eel. 
Yes. I want…                                          Shem. Fe vont…
Show me…                                             Orm mohn…
May I have a beg, please?                   Yame Fe vase E gach, Pleje?
Dissatisfied:   
Can you please exchange this?           Rom Ina pleje, Angeenj thes? 
I want to return this.                             Fe vont ote kombin thes.
I’d like a refund.                                     Fe’d kile E rogipe.
Here’s the receipt.                                Hech’s de yawrit.

Banks and Your Money:
Ponufers und Inar Segum:

Money in the Suquellish Tribes is authorized, coined, printed and released under the power of the Muda and specifically the Suquellish Montrasi treasury. Private banks owned by independent bankers, as seen in other nations around the plane is strictly prohibited by Suquellish Constitutional law. Furthermore, every Pon note and Trastel is by law backed by Silver and to a lesser extend, Gold. The Moolli Montrasi may only release in Pon notes and Trastels half the value of the Gold and Silver physically housed in the treasury.  This mean’s for every $100.00 dollars of gold or Silver actually, physically possessed by the Montrasi, they are only permitted by Law to allow $50.00 dollars in the form of Pon notes and Trastels into the general public circulation. Currently the exchange rate of the US dollar for Suquellish Pon is half, in favor of the Pon notes, which are backed mainly by silver, whereas the US dollar is a fait currency  backed by nothing other than the faith it’s user’s have placed in it and the fact it is the world’s reserve currency at present for oil purchases, making it backed by oil. Should the status of the US dollar change, however, it will have no backing at all and be deemed by the Suquellish Montrasi as worthless. As it is, the US dollar is already hyper-inflated by over printing and release. Therefore, the US Dollar on open exchange is worth only about half that of the Suquellish Pon. 
Understand, if you are holding dollars and wish to convert them into Pons, for every dollar you convert you will receive 50 Trastels. If you wish to convert your dollars into Pons you will only receive half as much in Pons, due to the Pon’s greater values determined by the spot prices of Silver and to a lesser extent Gold, in the international marketplace of Commerce. Should any nation’s currencies fail or become worthless, the Suquellish Republic shall also deem the currency worthless and refuse to accept it or exchange against it. This includes the UK Pound, The German Mark and the US, Australian and Canadian Dollar. There is no exception. Fait currency is of no value and Suquella operates on the Austrian system of economic laws and principles, not the Keynesian system of Credit and Debt for money generation.

HISTORY OF THE SUQUELISH REPUBLIC


The Suquelish Republic traces its origins to events that unfolded in 2012, rooted in questions of identity, belonging, and self-determination. That year, Marc Mason sought formal recognition within his native tribal community. Although he possessed extensive documentation verifying his lineage, he narrowly failed to meet the blood quantum requirements set by the Confederated Salish and Kootenai Tribes. While the Tribes informed him that he was ineligible for full membership, they extended limited benefits, including access to tribal medical insurance.
This decision deeply affected Mason, who viewed identity as something extending beyond administrative thresholds. Dissatisfied with the outcome, he pursued various avenues to challenge or reconsider the decision. During this period, he encountered the concept of micronations and the principles of international law that, in theory, permit their existence. Although he understood that such entities often lack formal recognition by established nation-states, Mason was intrigued by the symbolic and philosophical power of sovereignty, self-definition, and cultural autonomy.
Later in 2012, Mason founded the Suquelish Republic in Garden City, Idaho. His vision was to establish a new tribal community one open to individuals who, like himself, had been denied entry or full recognition within their ancestral tribes. The Suquelish Republic was conceived not merely as a political statement, but as a cultural project: a collective effort to create a distinct, inclusive people with their own traditions, values, and identity.
Interest in the project grew rapidly, and membership expanded. During this formative period, Mason’s then-girlfriend, Tia Bolton (now Tia Larson), originally from Washington and later residing in Pocatello, Idaho, was invited to design the national flag. After group discussion and deliberation, her design was formally adopted. The flag, rich in symbolism, became a central representation of Suquelish identity.
As the Republic developed, it established a range of internal civic institutions. The Suquelish Republic introduced its own community currency, intended for use among members and accepted at participating locations across several Idaho cities, including Boise, Meridian, Nampa, Lewiston, Moscow, and Coeur d’Alene. In addition, the Republic began issuing internal documentation such as passports, identification cards, and governmental records, including birth, marriage, and death certificates, to support its organizational structure.
A significant milestone occurred in 2015, when the Suquelish Republic entered into a mutual compact of recognition and independence with the Confederated Salish and Kootenai Tribes the very tribal body that had previously denied Mason full membership. That same year, the Suquelish Republic formally declared itself an independent, non-territorial sovereign entity, emphasizing its identity as a people rather than a land-based nation.
The Republic’s national symbols reflect both spiritual and cultural meaning. Its official animal is the lion and the lamb, representing strength and peace. The national colors green, white, red, and gold are prominently displayed on the flag. The international symbol consists of a half circle with three upward spikes, symbolizing the Father, the Son, and the Holy Spirit. The half circle represents the Shield of Faith, underscoring the Republic’s Christian theological foundation. For the Suquelish people, the flag serves not only as a national emblem but also as a profession of faith.
In 2022, the Suquelish Republic achieved another cultural milestone with the publication of its own language dictionary. The Suquelish Dykailum contains over 10,000 words, along with structured lessons, practice phrases, and example sentences. Today, members of the Republic read, write, and speak Suquelinese, using the language as a living expression of their shared identity.
Cultural life within the Suquelish Republic is marked by public festivals and gatherings. These events showcase Suquelish merchants, traditional recipes unique to the community, and music and dance inspired by the ancestral Native American roots of its members. While deeply cultural in nature, these festivals are open to the general public, reflecting the Republic’s commitment to visibility and engagement.
Today, the Suquelish Republic stands as a distinctive cultural community with its own language, symbols, customs, clothing, and traditions. Its people intentionally define themselves as set apart “strange and peculiar” existing outside the conventional structures of the nations of the earth. Through this deliberate separation, the Suquelish Republic continues to affirm its founding purpose: the creation of a unique people bound by shared experience, faith, and cultural self-determination.

Marc Matthew Mason: Creator and Founder of the Suquelish Republic

Jeffrey David Mason: Creator/Author of the Suquelish language (Suquelineese) and the dictionary called a: (Dykailum)
